<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

unaudited, condensed consolidated financial statements have been prepared
pursuant to rules and regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission
and, therefore, do not include all information and footnote disclosures
normally included in audited financial statements.&#160; However, in the opinion of management, all adjustments necessary
to present fairly the&nbsp;results of operations, financial position and cash
flows have been made.&#160; It is suggested
that these statements be read in conjunction with the financial statements
included in Abbott&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2003.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 3 - Taxes on
Earnings</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on earnings reflect
the estimated annual effective rates.&#160;
The effective tax rates are less than the statutory U.S. federal income
tax rate principally due to the benefit of tax exemptions in several taxing
jurisdictions and the domestic dividend exclusion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 4 - Litigation and
Environmental Matters</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott is involved in
various claims and legal proceedings including a number of antitrust suits and
investigations in connection with the pricing of prescription pharmaceuticals.
These suits and investigations allege that various pharmaceutical manufacturers
have conspired to fix prices for prescription pharmaceuticals and/or to
discriminate in pricing to retail pharmacies by providing discounts to
mail-order pharmacies, institutional pharmacies and HMOs in violation of state
and federal antitrust laws. The suits have been brought on behalf of retail
pharmacies and name certain pharmaceutical manufacturers, including Abbott, as
defendants. The cases seek treble damages, civil penalties, and injunctive and
other relief.&#160; Abbott has filed a
response to each of the complaints denying all substantive allegations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">There are several
lawsuits pending in connection with the sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Hytrin</font></i>. These suits allege
that Abbott violated state or federal antitrust laws and, in some cases, unfair
competition laws by signing patent settlement agreements with Geneva
Pharmaceuticals, Inc. and Zenith Laboratories, Inc. in 1998. Those agreements
related to pending patent infringement lawsuits between Abbott and the two
companies. Some of the suits also allege that Abbott violated various state or
federal laws by filing frivolous patent infringement lawsuits to protect <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Hytrin</font></i>
from generic competition. The cases seek treble damages, civil penalties and
other relief. Abbott has filed or intends to file a response to each of the
complaints denying all substantive allegations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott has been
identified as a potentially responsible party for investigation and cleanup
costs at a number of locations in the United States and Puerto Rico under
federal and state remediation laws and is investigating potential contamination
at a number of company-owned locations. Abbott has recorded an estimated cleanup
cost for each site for which management believes Abbott has a probable loss
exposure. No individual site cleanup exposure is expected to exceed
$3&nbsp;million, and the aggregate cleanup exposure is not expected to exceed
$20&nbsp;million.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">5</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='5',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Within the next year,
legal proceedings may occur that may result in a change in the estimated
reserves recorded by Abbott.&#160; For its
legal proceedings and environmental exposures discussed in this note and in
Note 5, Abbott estimates the
range of possible loss to be from approximately $120 million to $200 million.
Abbott has recorded reserves of approximately $135 million for these
proceedings and exposures.&#160; These
reserves represent management&#146;s best estimate of probable loss, as defined by
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;5, &#147;Accounting for
Contingencies.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While it is not feasible
to predict the outcome of all such proceedings and exposures with certainty,
management believes that their ultimate disposition should not have a material
adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial position, cash flows, or results of
operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 5 - TAP
Pharmaceutical Products Inc.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">TAP Pharmaceutical Products&nbsp;Inc. (TAP) and Abbott have been named
as defendants in several lawsuits alleging violations of various state or
federal laws in connection with TAP&#146;s marketing and pricing of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Lupron</font></i>. Abbott has filed or intends to
file a response to each of the lawsuits denying all substantive allegations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Within the next year, legal proceedings may occur that may result in a
change in the estimated reserves recorded by TAP and Abbott. While it is not
feasible to predict the outcome of such pending claims, proceedings, and
investigations with certainty, management is of the opinion that their ultimate
disposition should not have a material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial
position, cash flows, or results of operations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 6 - Post-Employment
Benefits</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Retirement plans consist of defined benefit, defined contribution, and
medical and dental plans. Net cost recognized for the three months ended
March&nbsp;31 for Abbott&#146;s major defined benefit plans and post-employment
medical and dental benefit plans is as follows:</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott funds its domestic defined benefit plans according to IRS
funding limitations.&#160; In the first
quarter of 2004, $200 million was contributed to the main domestic defined
benefit plan.&#160; Abbott expects to
contribute between $250 million and $300 million to its main domestic defined
benefit plan in 2004, including the contribution made in the first quarter
2004.</font></p>

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='6',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 7 &#150; Spin-off of
Abbott&#146;s Core Hospital Products Business</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In August&nbsp;2003,
Abbott announced a plan to create a separate publicly traded company for its
existing core hospital products business.&#160;
On April&nbsp;12, 2004, Abbott announced that its board of directors had
declared a special dividend distribution of all of the outstanding shares of
common stock of Hospira, Inc., the global hospital products company to be spun
off by Abbott.&#160; For every 10 shares of
Abbott common shares held at the close of business on April&nbsp;22, 2004,
Abbott shareholders will receive one share of Hospira stock.&#160; The special dividend distribution is
expected to be paid on April&nbsp;30, 2004.&#160;
Hospira will include the operations relating to the manufacture and sale
of hospital products including specialty injectable pharmaceuticals, medication
delivery systems and critical care devices and injectable pharmaceutical
contract manufacturing.&#160; Hospira will
include Abbott&#146;s Hospital Products segment and portions of Abbott&#146;s
International segment.&#160; All of the
shares of Hospira&#146;s common stock will be distributed to Abbott shareholders on
a pro-rata basis. Abbott has received a ruling from the Internal Revenue
Service that the spin-off qualifies as a tax-free distribution to Abbott and
its U.S. shareholders for U.S. federal income tax purposes.&#160; Cash, which will generally be taxable to the
recipient, will be issued in lieu of fractional shares.&#160; Hospira has filed a Form 10 with the
Securities and Exchange Commission, which includes 2003 unaudited pro forma
annual net sales of approximately $2.4 billion, unaudited pro forma annual
earnings before income taxes of approximately $360 million and annual net cash
flow from operating and investing activities of approximately $175 million.&#160; Subsequent to the spin-off, the financial
results of Hospira and the costs of the spin-off will be presented as
discontinued operations in Abbott&#146;s financial statements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In April 2004, Abbott
borrowed and Hospira will assume approximately $700 million of debt, the
proceeds of which will be retained by Abbott to reduce short-term
borrowings.&#160; Hospira will be solely
responsible for repayment of the principal and for payment of interest on this
debt.&#160; The legal transfer of certain
operations and assets (net of liabilities) outside the United States will occur
after the distribution date.&#160; These
operations and assets will be used in the conduct of Hospira&#146;s international
business and Hospira will be subject to the risks and entitled to the benefits
generated by these operations and assets commencing immediately after the
distribution date.&#160; In accordance with
the contracts covering the spin-off, Abbott will retain liabilities for taxes
on income prior to the spin-off, post-employment medical benefits for most of
Hospira&#146;s U. S. retired employees and U. S. retirement eligible employees,
certain potential liabilities, if any, related to alleged improper pricing
practices in connection with federal, state and private reimbursement for
certain drugs, and the defined benefit retirement plan liabilities and plan
assets for most of Hospira&#146;s retired employees.&#160; Hospira employees who are eligible to retire as of the spin-off
date and who hold options on Abbott common shares will be considered retired
for purposes of those outstanding options.&#160;
Options held by Hospira employees who are not eligible to retire will be
cancelled and replaced with Hospira options.&#160;
Abbott options and Hospira options that replace Abbott options will be
adjusted for the effects of the spin-off on the value of the options.&#160;&#160; An Information Statement including a copy
of Hospira&#146;s Form 10 for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003, was mailed to
Abbott shareholders as of the record date.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 9 - Segment
Information <i><font style="font-style:italic;">(dollars
in millions)</font></i></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Revenue Segments</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; Abbott&#146;s principal business is the discovery,
development, manufacture and sale of a broad line of health care products.&#160; Abbott&#146;s products are generally sold
directly to retailers, wholesalers, hospitals, health care facilities,
laboratories, physicians&#146; offices and government agencies throughout the
world.&#160; Effective January&nbsp;1, 2004,
Abbott&#146;s segments were reorganized to reflect the shift of certain hospital
pharmaceutical products from the Hospital Products segment to the
Pharmaceutical Products segment, and the separation of the vascular and spinal
products businesses into non-reportable segments.&#160; After this reorganization, only the domestic core hospital
businesses that are expected to be spun off to Hospira are reported in the
Hospital Products segment.&#160; In addition,
as of January&nbsp;1, 2004, the Diagnostic Products segment was reorganized
into four separate divisions.&#160; For
segment reporting purposes, these divisions are collectively reported as the
Diagnostic Products segment.&#160; The
segment information below has been restated to reflect these
reorganizations.&#160; Abbott&#146;s reportable
segments are as follows:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Pharmaceutical Products</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; U.S. sales of a broad line of pharmaceuticals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Diagnostic Products</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; Worldwide sales of diagnostic systems and tests for
blood banks, hospitals, consumers, commercial laboratories and alternate-care
testing sites.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Hospital Products</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; U.S. sales of hospital products, including specialty
injectable pharmaceuticals, medication delivery systems and critical care
devices and injectable pharmaceutical contract manufacturing.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Ross Products</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; U.S. sales of a broad line of adult and pediatric
nutritional products, pediatric pharmaceuticals and consumer products.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">International</font></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; Non-U.S. sales of all of Abbott&#146;s pharmaceutical,
hospital and nutritional products. Products sold by International are
manufactured by domestic segments and by international manufacturing locations.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">8</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='8',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s underlying
accounting records are maintained on a legal entity basis for government and
public reporting requirements. Segment disclosures are on a performance basis
consistent with internal management reporting. Intersegment transfers of
inventory are recorded at standard cost and are not a measure of segment operating
earnings. The cost of some corporate functions and the cost of certain employee
benefits are sold to segments at predetermined rates that approximate cost.
Remaining costs, if any, are not allocated to segments. Intangible assets and
related amortization from business acquisitions are not allocated to segments.
The following segment information has been prepared in accordance with the
internal accounting policies of Abbott, as described above, and are not
presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles applied
to the consolidated financial statements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In connection with the
reorganization of the Hospital Products segment, as described above, certain
assets previously included in the Hospital Products segment have been
transferred to other segments resulting in a decrease in the total assets in
the Hospital Products segment from $2,153 at December&nbsp;31, 2003 to $1,604
at March&nbsp;31, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 10 &#150; Sale of Product
Rights</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the first quarter 2003, Abbott completed the sale
of its U.S. eye and ear care product lines and recorded this transaction in net
sales in accordance with Abbott&#146;s revenue recognition accounting policies as
discussed in Note 1 to the financial statements included in Abbott&#146;s Annual
Report on Form 10-K.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 11 &#150; Business Combinations</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In January&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired i-STAT
Corporation, a manufacturer of point-of-care diagnostic products for blood
analysis, for approximately $394 million in cash.&#160; In the first quarter of 2004, Abbott recorded a charge of
approximately $60 million for acquired in-process research and development,
intangible assets of approximately $263 million and non-tax deductible goodwill
of approximately $138 million, which is subject to the completion of an
independent appraisal that is expected to be completed in the second quarter of
2004.&#160; Acquired intangible assets,
primarily product technology, will be amortized over 7 to 18 years (average of
approximately 17 years).&#160; Had the
acquisition taken place on January&nbsp;1 of the previous year, consolidated
sales and income would not have been significantly different from reported
amounts.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In April&nbsp;2004,
Abbott acquired TheraSense, Inc., a leader in the development, manufacturing
and marketing of blood glucose self-monitoring systems, for approximately $1.2
billion in cash.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 12 &#150; Incentive Stock
Programs</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott measures compensation cost using the intrinsic value-based
method of accounting for stock options and replacement options granted to
employees. Had compensation cost been determined using the fair value-based
accounting method, pro forma net income (<i><font style="font-style:italic;">in
millions</font></i>) and earnings per share (EPS) amounts would have been as

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 13 &#150; Equity Method
Investment</font></p>

Products&nbsp;Inc. (TAP), is accounted for under the equity method of
accounting.&#160; Abbott&#146;s income from the
TAP joint venture is recognized net of consolidating adjustments. Summarized
financial information for TAP is as follows:</font></p>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 14 &#150; Long-term Debt and Interest Rate Hedge
Contracts</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under a registration
statement filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission in
September&nbsp;2003, Abbott issued $1.5 billion of long-term debt in the first
quarter of 2004 that matures in 2009 through 2014 with interest rates ranging
from 3.5 percent to 4.35 percent.&#160;
Proceeds from this debt were used to fund the acquisition of TheraSense
in the second quarter of 2004 and to pay down domestic commercial paper
borrowings.&#160; In connection with these
borrowings, Abbott entered into interest rate hedge contracts totaling $1.5
billion to manage its exposure to changes in the fair value of the $1.5 billion
of debt.&#160; These contracts are designated
as fair value hedges of the variability of the fair value of fixed-rate debt
due to changes in the long-term bench-mark interest rates.&#160; The effect of the hedge is to change the
fixed interest rate to a variable rate.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note&nbsp;15&nbsp;</font>&#150; Goodwill and Intangible Assets</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in
millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott recorded goodwill of $138 related to the acquisition of i-STAT
in the first quarter of 2004. &#160;Foreign
currency translation adjustments increased goodwill in the first quarters of
2004 and 2003 by approximately $132 and $248, respectively.&#160; There were no reductions of goodwill
relating to impairments or disposal of all or a portion of a business.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The gross amount of amortizable intangible assets, primarily product
rights and technology, was $5,194 as of March&nbsp;31, 2004 and $4,841 as of
December&nbsp;31, 2003, and accumulated amortization was $955 as of
March&nbsp;31, 2004 and $899 as of December&nbsp;31, 2003.&#160; The net amount of intangible assets with
indefinite lives, primarily registered trade names, not subject to amortization
was $148 at March&nbsp;31, 2004 and December&nbsp;31, 2003.&#160; The estimated annual amortization expense
for intangible assets, including amortization of intangibles related to the
TheraSense acquisition, is $429 in 2004, $436 in 2005, $433 in 2006, $420 in
2007, and $397 in 2008.&#160; Intangible
assets are amortized primarily on a straight-line basis over 4 to 25&nbsp;years
(average 14&nbsp;years).</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">11</font></p>

  <p align="right" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1,816</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="2%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:2.0%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="12%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:12.0%;">
  <p align="right" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17.7</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="1%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:1.0%;">
  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</table>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a) Percentage changes
are based on unrounded numbers</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Worldwide sales for the
first quarter 2004 reflect primarily unit growth and the positive effect of the
relatively weaker U.S. dollar.&#160; The
relatively weaker U.S. dollar increased first quarter 2004 consolidated net
sales 4.9 percent and increased international sales 12.4 percent over the first
quarter 2003.&#160; In addition, the effect
of the relatively weaker U.S. dollar increased 2004 sales in the Diagnostic
Products and International segments by 8.2 percent and 13.2 percent,
respectively.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">12</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a) Percentage changes are based on unrounded numbers.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Increased sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Flomax</font></i>,
<i><font style="font-style:italic;">Synthroid</font></i>
and <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Tricor</font></i>
in 2004 favorably impacted the Primary Care product sales of the Pharmaceutical
Products segment, and increased sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i>
favorably impacted Specialty products sales.&#160;
Diagnostic Products and International segment product sales were
favorably impacted in 2004 and 2003 by the effect of the relatively weaker U.S.
dollar.&#160; Worldwide sales of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i> totaled $149&nbsp;million in the
first quarter 2004 and are forecasted to be more than $700&nbsp;million for the
full year 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The gross profit margin
was 52.4&nbsp;percent for the first quarter 2004 compared to 52.0 percent for
the first quarter 2003.&#160; This increase
was due primarily to favorable product sales mix, reflecting a relatively
higher sales contribution from the Pharmaceutical Products segment, and price
and was partially offset by the unfavorable mix effect of exchange on the gross
profit margin and higher manufacturing costs.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Research and development
expenses for the first quarter 2004 increased 5.7 percent over 2003 due, in
part, to increased spending to support pipeline programs, such as the follow-on
indications for <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira, </font></i>other late-stage clinical programs in
pharmaceuticals, vascular devices and molecular diagnostics.&#160; The majority of research and development
expenditures are concentrated on pharmaceutical products.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">13</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='13',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Selling, general and administrative
expenses for the first quarter 2004 increased 21.9 percent over 2003.&#160; The increase is due primarily to increased
selling and marketing support for new and existing products, including
continued spending on the launch of <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Humira</font></i>,
as well as spending on other global pharmaceutical branded products and
domestic nutritionals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Business Combinations</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In January&nbsp;2004, Abbott acquired i-STAT
Corporation, a manufacturer of point-of-care diagnostic products for blood
analysis, for approximately $394 million in cash.&#160; In the first quarter of 2004, Abbott recorded a charge of
approximately $60 million for acquired in-process research and development,
intangible assets of approximately $263 million and non-tax deductible goodwill
of approximately $138 million, which is subject to the completion of an
independent appraisal that is expected to be completed in the second quarter of
2004.&#160; Acquired intangible assets,
primarily product technology, will be amortized over 7 to 18 years (average of
approximately 17 years).&#160; Had the
acquisition taken place on January&nbsp;1 of the previous year, consolidated
sales and income would not have been significantly different from reported
amounts.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In April&nbsp;2004,
Abbott acquired TheraSense, Inc., a leader in the development, manufacturing
and marketing of blood glucose self-monitoring systems, for approximately $1.2
billion in cash.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Spin-off of Abbott&#146;s Core
Hospital Products Business</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In August&nbsp;2003,
Abbott announced a plan to create a separate publicly traded company for its existing
core hospital products business.&#160; On
April&nbsp;12, 2004, Abbott announced that its board of directors had declared
a special dividend distribution of all of the outstanding shares of common
stock of Hospira, Inc., the global hospital products company to be spun off by
Abbott.&#160; For every 10 shares of Abbott
common shares held at the close of business on April&nbsp;22, 2004, Abbott
shareholders will receive one share of Hospira stock.&#160; The special dividend distribution is expected to be paid on
April&nbsp;30, 2004.&#160; Hospira will
include the operations relating to the manufacture and sale of hospital
products including specialty injectable pharmaceuticals, medication delivery
systems and critical care devices and injectable pharmaceutical contract
manufacturing.&#160; Hospira will include
Abbott&#146;s Hospital Products segment and portions of Abbott&#146;s International
segment.&#160; All of the shares of Hospira&#146;s
common stock will be distributed to Abbott shareholders on a pro-rata basis.
Abbott has received a ruling from the Internal Revenue Service that the
spin-off qualifies as a tax-free distribution to Abbott and its U.S.
shareholders for U.S. federal income tax purposes.&#160; Cash, which will generally be taxable to the recipient, will be
issued in lieu of fractional shares.&#160;
Hospira has filed a Form 10 with the Securities and Exchange Commission,
which includes 2003 unaudited pro forma annual net sales of approximately $2.4
billion, unaudited pro forma annual earnings before income taxes of
approximately $360 million and annual net cash flow from operating and
investing activities of approximately $175 million.&#160; Subsequent to the spin-off, the financial results of Hospira and
the costs of the spin-off will be presented as discontinued operations in
Abbott&#146;s financial statements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In April 2004, Abbott
borrowed and Hospira will assume approximately $700 million of debt, the
proceeds of which will be retained by Abbott to reduce short-term
borrowings.&#160; Hospira will be solely
responsible for repayment of the principal and for payment of interest on this
debt.&#160; The legal transfer of certain
operations and assets (net of liabilities) outside the United States will occur
after the distribution date.&#160; These
operations and assets will be used in the conduct of Hospira&#146;s international
business and Hospira will be subject to the risks and entitled to the benefits
generated by these operations and assets commencing immediately after the
distribution date.&#160; In accordance with
the contracts covering the spin-off, Abbott will retain liabilities for taxes
on income prior to the spin-off, post-employment medical benefits for most of
Hospira&#146;s U. S. retired employees and U. S. retirement eligible employees,
certain potential liabilities, if any, related to alleged improper pricing
practices in connection with federal, state and private reimbursement for
certain drugs, and the defined benefit retirement plan liabilities and plan
assets for most of Hospira&#146;s retired employees.&#160; Hospira employees who are eligible to retire as of the spin-off
date and who hold options on Abbott common shares will be considered retired
for purposes of those outstanding options.&#160;
Options held by Hospira employees who are not eligible to retire will be
cancelled and replaced with Hospira options.&#160;
Abbott options and Hospira options that replace Abbott options will be
adjusted for the effects of the spin-off on the value of the options.&#160;&#160; An Information Statement including a copy
of Hospira&#146;s Form 10 for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2003, was mailed to
Abbott shareholders as of the record date.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">14</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net Interest Expense</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net interest expense
decreased in the first quarter of 2004 compared to 2003 due primarily to lower
interest rates.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Sale of Product Rights</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the first quarter
2003, Abbott completed the sale of its U.S. eye and ear care product lines and
recorded this transaction in net sales in accordance with Abbott&#146;s revenue
recognition accounting policies as discussed in Note 1 to the financial
statements included in Abbott&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K.&#160; Related gains recorded in net sales were not
significant to consolidated net sales.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on Earnings</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on earnings reflect
the estimated annual effective rates and, for 2004, include the effect of the
charge for non-deductible acquired in-process research and development relating
to the acquisition of i-STAT.&#160; The
effect of this charge was to increase the effective tax rate from 24.5 percent
to 25.8 percent.&#160; Abbott anticipates
that the effective tax rate for the rest of 2004 will be higher than 24.5
percent due to the effect of the charge for non-deductible acquired in-process
research and development relating to the acquisition of TheraSense in the
second quarter of 2004.&#160; The effective
tax rates, excluding the effect of these charges, are less than the statutory
U.S.&nbsp;federal income tax rate principally due to the benefit of tax
exemptions in several taxing jurisdictions and the domestic dividend exclusion.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Liquidity and Capital
Resources at March&nbsp;31, 2004 Compared with December&nbsp;31, 2003</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net cash from operating
activities for the first quarter 2004 totaled $1.4 billion. Abbott expects
annual cash flow from operating activities to continue to exceed Abbott&#146;s
capital expenditures and cash dividends.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At March&nbsp;31, 2004,
Abbott had working capital of approximately $4.0 billion compared to working
capital of approximately $2.7&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2003.&#160; The increase in working capital in 2004 was
primarily due to the reduction of short-term commercial paper borrowings with
proceeds from the issuance of long-term debt and operating cash flows used to
increase short-term investment securities.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At March&nbsp;31, 2004,
Abbott&#146;s long-term debt rating was AA by Standard &amp; Poor&#146;s Corporation and
A1 by Moody&#146;s Investors Service. Abbott has readily available financial
resources, including unused lines of credit of $3.0 billion, which support
commercial paper borrowing arrangements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In June&nbsp;2000, the
Board of Directors authorized the purchase of 25 million shares of Abbott&#146;s
common stock and Abbott purchased 10.6 million shares from this authorization
in 2001 and 2000.&#160; Common stock
purchases were temporarily suspended in January&nbsp;2001, following Abbott&#146;s
announced acquisition of the pharmaceutical business of BASF.&#160; In 2003, Abbott announced that it plans to
purchase the remaining 14.4 million shares from time to time on the open market
and purchased 2.7 million of its common shares at a cost of $98 million.&#160; During the first quarter 2004, Abbott purchased
6.9 million of its common shares at a cost of $297 million.&#160; As of March&nbsp;31, 2004, an additional 4.8
million shares may be purchased in future periods under the June&nbsp;2000
authorization by the Board of Directors.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the first quarter 2004, $200 million was contributed to Abbott&#146;s
main domestic defined benefit plan. Abbott expects to contribute between $250
million and $300 million to its main domestic defined benefit plan in 2004,
including the contribution made in the first quarter 2004.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">15</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='15',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under a registration
statement filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission in
September&nbsp;2003, Abbott issued $1.5 billion of long-term debt in the first
quarter of 2004 that matures in 2009 through 2014 with interest rates ranging
from 3.5 percent to 4.35 percent.&#160;
Proceeds from this debt were used to fund the acquisition of TheraSense
in the second quarter of 2004 and to pay down domestic commercial paper
borrowings.&#160; In connection with these
borrowings, Abbott entered into interest rate hedge contracts totaling $1.5
billion to manage its exposure to changes in the fair value of the $1.5 billion
of debt.&#160; These contracts are designated
as fair value hedges of the variability of the fair value of fixed-rate debt due
to changes in the long-term bench-mark interest rates.&#160; The effect of the hedge is to change the
fixed interest rate to a variable rate.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott will fund maturing
long-term debt of $1.65 billion, due in July&nbsp;2004, out of operating cash
flows and domestic commercial paper borrowing.&#160;
In addition, Abbott expects to retain approximately $700 million of
proceeds from borrowings that will be assumed by Hospira as a result of the
spin-off of Hospira.&#160; Abbott intends to
use these proceeds to reduce short-term borrowings.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Legislative Issues</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s primary markets
are highly competitive and subject to comprehensive government regulation.&#160; Abbott expects debate to continue at both
the federal and the state levels over the availability, method of delivery, and
payment for health care products and&nbsp;services.&#160; Abbott believes that if legislation were to be enacted, it could
have the effect of reducing prices, or reducing the rate of price increases for
health care products and services.&#160;
International operations are also subject to a significant degree of
government regulation.&#160; It is not
possible to predict the extent to which Abbott or the health care industry in
general might be adversely affected by these factors in the future.&#160; A more complete discussion of&nbsp;these
factors is contained in Item 1, Business, in the Annual&nbsp;Report on
Form&nbsp;10-K, which is available upon request.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Private Securities
Litigation Reform Act of 1995 &#151; A Caution Concerning Forward-Looking Statements</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under the safe harbor
provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995, Abbott
cautions investors that any forward-looking statements or projections made by
Abbott, including those made in this document, are subject to risks and
uncertainties that may cause actual results to differ materially from those
projected. Economic, competitive, governmental, technological and other factors
that may affect Abbott&#146;s operations are discussed in Exhibit 99.1 to the Annual
Report on Form&nbsp;10-K.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PART
I.&#160; FINANCIAL INFORMATION</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item
4.</font></u><b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160; </font></b><u><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Controls and Procedures</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .75in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Evaluation
of disclosure controls and procedures.&#160; </font></i>The
Chief Executive Officer, Miles D. White, and Chief Financial Officer, Thomas C.
Freyman, evaluated the effectiveness of Abbott Laboratories&#146; disclosure
controls and procedures as of the end of the period covered by this report, and
concluded that Abbott Laboratories&#146; disclosure controls and procedures were
effective to ensure that information Abbott is required to disclose in its
filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission under the Securities
Exchange Act of 1934 is recorded, processed, summarized and reported, within
the time periods specified in the Commission&#146;s rules and forms, and to ensure
that information required to be disclosed by Abbott in the reports that it
files under the Exchange Act is accumulated and communicated to Abbott&#146;s
management, including its principal executive officer and principal financial
officer, as appropriate to allow timely decisions regarding required
disclosure.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h1 style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:normal;">PART II.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; OTHER INFORMATION</font></b></h1>

<h1 style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></b></h1>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 47.9pt;text-indent:-47.9pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 1.</font></u>&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; <u>Legal Proceedings</u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 47.9pt;text-indent:-47.9pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott is
involved in various claims, legal proceedings and investigations, including (as
of March 31, 2004, except as otherwise indicated) those described below.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2003
Form 10-K, Abbott reported that three cases were pending in which Abbott sought
to protect its patents for divalproex sodium (a drug that Abbott sells under
the trademark Depakote&#174;).&#160; In the case
against TorPharm, a division of Apotex, Inc. (&#147;TorPharm&#148;), the United States
District Court for the Northern District of Illinois ruled in Abbott&#146;s favor in
March 2004 finding that TorPharm&#146;s proposed product infringed Abbott&#146;s patents
and entered an injunction effective March 31, 2004:&#160; (i) barring TorPharm and its affiliates from commercially
manufacturing, using, selling, or offering to sell in the United States the
generic divalproex sodium product found to be infringing or from importing that
product into the United States until Abbott&#146;s patents expire and TorPharm
receives final approval from the Food and Drug Administration (FDA), and (ii)
directing that the effective date of any approval by FDA of the Abbreviated New
Drug Application, or any other application concerning the divalproex sodium product
that was found to be infringing, shall be no earlier than January 29, 2008, the
date Abbott&#146;s patents expire.&#160; In April
2004, TorPharm filed a Notice of Appeal.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As previously
reported, a number of cases brought as purported class actions or representative
actions on behalf of individuals or entities, are pending that allege generally
that Abbott and numerous other pharmaceutical companies reported false pricing
information in connection with certain drugs that are reimbursable under
Medicare and Medicaid.&#160; These cases,
brought by private plaintiffs and State Attorneys General, generally seek
damages, treble damages, disgorgement of profits, restitution and attorneys&#146;
fees.&#160; The federal court cases have been
consolidated in the United States District Court in Massachusetts under the
Multidistrict Litigation Rules as <i><font style="font-style:italic;">In
re:&#160; Pharmaceutical Industry Average
Wholesale Price Litigation, MDL 1456.&#160; </font></i>Plaintiffs
in <i><font style="font-style:italic;">MDL 1456</font></i> also allege that
defendants inflated prices on drugs sold through pharmacy benefit managers and
allege price fixing by certain defendants, including Abbott, in the creation in
2002 of TogetherRx, LLC, a drug discount program for poor, elderly
Americans.&#160; The following previously
reported cases have been transferred to <i><font style="font-style:italic;">MDL
1456:&#160; County of Westchester, Digel,
State of California ex rel. Ven-A-Care of the Florida Keys </font></i>and <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Turner.</font></i> One of the previously reported
federal court cases, <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Rice, </font></i>has
been dismissed without prejudice.&#160; Two
additional state court cases have been filed:&#160;
<i><font style="font-style:italic;">Commonwealth of Pennsylvania v. TAP
Pharmaceutical Products, Inc., et al, </font></i>filed March 10, 2004, in the
Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania and <i><font style="font-style:italic;">State
of Ohio v. Dey, Inc.,</font></i>  <i><font style="font-style:italic;">et al, </font></i>filed
March 9, 2004, in the Court of Common Pleas, Hamilton County,</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">18</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='18',FILE='C:\jms\ajanaki\04-4788-1\task116147\4788-1-bc.htm',USER='kranganathan',CD='Apr 29 06:32 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Ohio.&#160; Abbott has filed or intends to file a response in each case
denying all substantive allegations.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A number of
cases have been brought against TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc., Abbott and
Takeda Chemical Industries, Ltd. in various courts that generally allege that
TAP reported false pricing information in connection with Lupron&#174;, a product
reimbursable under Medicare.&#160; The
previously reported federal court cases have been consolidated in the United
States District Court in Massachusetts under the Multidistrict Litigation Rules
as <i><font style="font-style:italic;">In re:&#160;
Lupron&#174; Marketing and Sales Practices Litigation, MDL 1430,</font></i>
and include (i) a consolidated class action complaint brought on behalf of all
persons or entities who paid for Lupron&#174; at a price calculated by reference to
the published average wholesale price from January 1, 1991 through September
2001; (ii) <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Empire Healthchoice, Inc., et
al., v. TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc., Abbott Laboratories and Takeda
Chemical Industries, Ltd., </font></i>filed in June 2002 in the United States
District Court in Massachusetts; (iii) <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Cobalt
Corporation v. Abbott Laboratories, Inc., Takeda Chemical Industries Ltd. and
TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc., </font></i>filed in August 2002 in the United
States District Court in Massachusetts; (iv) <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Health
Care Service Corporation v. TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc., et al., </font></i>removed
to the Eastern District of Texas in March 2003; and (v) <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Liberty National Life Ins. Co. et al. v. TAP
Pharmaceutical Products Inc., et al., </font></i>filed in the Northern District
of Alabama in October 2003.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As reported in
the 2003 Form 10-K, Abbott is a defendant in numerous lawsuits involving the
drug oxycodone (a drug sold under the trademark OxyContin&#174;), which is
manufactured by Purdue Pharma.&#160; Abbott
promoted OxyContin to certain specialty physicians, including surgeons and
anesthesiologists, under a co-promotion agreement with Purdue Pharma.&#160; Purdue Pharma is a defendant in each lawsuit
and, pursuant to the co-promotion agreement, Purdue is required to indemnify
Abbott in each lawsuit.&#160; Most of the
lawsuits allege generally that plaintiffs suffered personal injuries as a
result of taking OxyContin.&#160; A few
lawsuits allege consumer protection violations and unfair trade practices. One
suit by a third party payor alleges antitrust pricing violations and
overpricing of the drug.&#160; One case has
been brought by the Attorney General for the State of West Virginia.&#160; As of March 31, 2004, there are a total of
314 lawsuits pending in which Abbott is a party.&#160; 52 cases are pending in federal court; 262 cases are pending in
state court. 287 cases are brought by individual plaintiffs, and 27 cases are
brought as purported class action lawsuits.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:31.5pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2003 Form 10-K, Abbott reported that three shareholder
derivative actions were consolidated and pending in the Circuit Court of Cook
County, Illinois related to the resolution of the enteral nutritional
investigation.&#160; The suits allege that
the directors breached their fiduciary duties in failing to stop the alleged
improper business practices in the enteral nutritional business.&#160; One of the plaintiffs, Ted Gordon, was
elected lead</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">19</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">plaintiff, and an amended
complaint was filed on March 29, 2004.&#160;
Abbott and the directors deny all substantive allegations and intend to
move to dismiss the cases.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:31.5pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2003
Form 10-K, Abbott reported that it is a defendant in a number of lawsuits
involving the drug sibutramine (sold under the trademark Meridia&#174;) that have
been brought either as purported class actions or on behalf of individual
plaintiffs.&#160; The lawsuits generally
allege design defects and failure to warn.&#160;
Certain lawsuits also allege consumer protection violations and/or
unfair trade practices.&#160; As of March 31,
2004, 123 lawsuits were pending in which Abbott is a party.&#160; 114 cases are being or have been transferred
to the United States District Court for the Southern District of Ohio and are
captioned, <i><font style="font-style:italic;">In Re Meridia MDL No. 1481</font></i>.&#160; Seven cases are pending in state court, one
case in pending in Canada, and one case in pending in Italy.&#160; One additional state court case was filed
during the first quarter:&#160; <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Lemetti</font></i>, filed in March 2004 in the
Circuit Court, Cook County, Illinois.&#160;
The previously dismissed case in Italy, <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Casartelli
v. Abbott, et al., </font></i>was refiled on February 19, 2004 in the Court of
Milan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott is
involved in two cases against Teva Pharmaceuticals USA, Inc. related to
Abbott&#146;s patents for clarithromycin (a drug Abbott sells under the trademarks
Biaxin&#174; and Biaxin XL&#174;).&#160; Teva filed a
declaratory judgment action in the Northern District of Illinois alleging that
Teva&#146;s proposed immediate release formulation of Biaxin&#174; does not infringe
certain Abbott patents and that Abbott&#146;s patents are invalid.&#160; Abbott counterclaimed that Teva&#146;s proposed
product would infringe Abbott&#146;s patents.&#160;
Teva filed a separate declaratory judgment action in the Northern
District of Illinois alleging that its proposed extended release formulation of
Biaxin XL&#174; does not infringe any valid Abbott patent.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While it is not feasible to predict the
outcome of such pending claims, proceedings and investigations with certainty,
management is of the opinion that their ultimate dispositions should not have a
material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial position, cash flows, or results
of operations.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 6.</font></u>&#160;&#160;&#160; <u>Exhibits and Reports on Form 8-K</u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; Exhibits</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 47.9pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 73.45pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Incorporated by reference to the Exhibit Index included herewith.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 47.9pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; Reports
on Form 8-K</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 47.9pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 73.45pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On January 16, 2004, Abbott Laboratories furnished a Current Report on
Securities and Exchange Commission Form 8-K reporting the press release issued
by Abbott Laboratories that announced Abbott&#146;s results of operations for the
fourth quarter and full year of 2003.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 73.45pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On April 6, 2004, Abbott filed a Current Report on Securities and
Exchange Commission Form 8-K reporting that Abbott has adjusted its business
segment reporting to reflect segment reclassifications effective January 1,
2004 as a result of shifts of reporting responsibilities for certain products
previously included in U.S. Hospital Products Sales.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 73.45pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On April 8, 2004, Abbott Laboratories furnished a Current Report on
Securities and Exchange Commission Form 8-K reporting the press release issued
by Abbott Laboratories that announced Abbott&#146;s results of operations for the
first quarter of 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">NOTE:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For
the purpose of calculating this ratio, (i) earnings have been calculated by
adjusting net earnings for taxes on earnings; interest expense; amortization of
capitalized interest, net of capitalized interest; minority interest; and the
portion of rentals representative of the interest factor, (ii) Abbott considers
one-third of rental expense to be the amount representing return on capital,
and (iii) fixed charges comprise total interest expense, including capitalized
interest and such portion of rentals.</font></p>

<h2 style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;text-indent:0in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></b></h2>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In connection
with the Quarterly Report of Abbott Laboratories (the &#147;Company&#148;) on Form 10-Q
for the period ended March 31, 2004 as filed with the Securities and Exchange
Commission (the &#147;Report&#148;), I, Miles D. White, Chairman of the Board and Chief
Executive Officer of the Company, certify, pursuant to 18 U.S.C. &#167; 1350, as
adopted pursuant to &#167; 906 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, that:</font></p>

Securities Exchange Act of 1934; and</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(2)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The
